Council of the County of Maui  on 2023-02-17 9:00 AM - Regular Meeting
[ GAVEL ] WILL THE MAUI COUNTY COUNCIL REGULAR MEETING OF FEBRUARY 17TH, 2023 PLEASE 
CONVENE. LET ME SAY THAT ONE MORE TIME. WILL THE COUNCIL MEETING OF FEBRUARY 17TH, 
2023 PLEASE CONVENE. IT IS 9:00 A.M. ON FRIDAY. MEMBERS, AS WE DO ROLL CALL, THE GOOD 
MORNING GREETING IS TALOFA. MS. CLERK. \r\n\r\n>> THANK YOU, CHAIR. TALOFA. PROCEEDING 
WITH ROLL CALL, MEMBERS PARTICIPATING FROM NON-PUBLIC LOCATIONS SHOULD STATE, WHO 
IF ANYONE, EXCEPT MINORS, IS PRESENT WITH THEM AS PART OF ROLL CALL. COUNCIL MEMBER 
TASHA KAMA. >> TALOFA CHAIR AND FELLOW COLLEAGUES. IT'S GREAT TO BE HOME AND GREAT 
TO BE AMONG ALL OF YOU AND LOOK FORWARD TO A VERY PRODUCTIVE AND EXPEDITIOUS 
MEETING TODAY. THANK YOU.\r\n\r\n>> COUNCIL MEMBER YUKI LEI SUGIMURA. >> TALOFA 
EVERYBODY. IT'S GOOD TO BE IN THE COUNCIL CHAMBERS WITH MY FELLOW COUNCIL MEMBERS 
AND STAFF. THANK YOU VERY MUCH ALL OF YOU WHO WEATHERED THE STORM. GOOD 
MORNING. >> COUNCIL MEMBER TAMARA PALTIN. >> GOOD MORNING.\r\n\r\n>> TALOFA AND 
ALOHA KAKAHIAKA AND BROADCASTING LIVE AND DIRECT FROM HISTORIC LAHAINA TOWN, 
WHERE IT'S FULL-ON RAIN OVER HERE. I DIDN'T FEEL SAFE ENOUGH TO DRIVE AFTER LAST NIGHT. 
SO JUST STAYING IN THE WEST DISTRICT. THANK YOU. OH, AND I HAVE WITH ME LAHAINA 
DISTRICT OFFICE STAFF CRISTEN BOLANOS. >> THANK YOU. >> COUNCIL MEMBER GABE 
JOHNSON.\r\n\r\n>> TALOFA, CHAIR, COUNCIL MEMBERS, COMMUNITY MEMBERS. I'M HERE TODAY, 
READY TO WORK. THERE ARE NO TESTIFIERS AT THE LANA'I DISTRICT OFFICE AND I HOPE 
EVERYBODY IN THIS RAINY TIME TAKE CARE OF THEMSELVES AND TAKE CARE OF THEIR 
PROPERTY, BUT DON'T FORGET YOUR PETS OF THE JUST SAYING THAT. THANK YOU, CHAIR. >> 
COUNCIL MEMBER KEANI RAWLINS-FERNANDEZ. >> ALOHA KAKAHIAKA, CHAIR. AND 
MEMBERS.\r\n\r\nAND OUR PUBLIC. I'M HERE AT THE MOLOKA'I DISTRICT OFFICE, ALONE ON MY 
SIDE OF THE OFFICE, AND OUR COMMUNITY OUTREACH SPECIALIST ZHANTELL LINDO IS ON THE 
OTHER SIDE OF THE OFFICE, NOT BEING THERE IN PERSON WITH YOU ALL LIKE MEMBER PALTIN, 
WASN'T SAFE WITH THIS STORM AND I DIDN'T WANT NOT TO BE ABLE TO RETURN HOME AND 
THERE ARE NO TESTIFIERS HERE AT MOLOKA'I DISTRICT OFFICE AT THIS TIME. MAHALO, CHAIR. >>  
THANK YOU. COUNCIL MEMBER TOM COOK? >> TALOFA, CHAIR AND COUNCIL MEMBERS. HAPPY 
TO BE HERE AND READY TO GO TO WORK.\r\n\r\n>> COUNCIL MEMBER NOHELANI UU-HODGINS. >> 
TALOFA AND GOOD MORNING. >> GOOD MORNING. >> COUNCIL MEMBER SHANE SINENCI. >> 
ALOHA KAKAHIAKA CHAIR AND TALOFA AND STAFF MENTIONED THERE'S NO MEMBERS AT THE 
DISTRICT OFFICE. >> COUNCIL CHAIR ALICE LEE. >> TALOFA EVERYONE AND LOOKING FORWARD 
TO A VERY PRODUCTIVE MEETING, AND VERY EFFICIENT ONE, LIKE MEMBER KAMA 
SAID.\r\n\r\nTHANK YOU. >> CHAIR, THERE ARE NINE MEMBERS PRESENT, NO MEMBERS ARE 
ABSENT. AND A QUORUM IS PRESENT TO CONDUCT THE BUSINESS OF THE COUNCIL. FOR THE 
RECORD, I'M DEPUTY COUNTY CLERK RICHELLE THOMSON AND ALSO HERE IS COUNTY CLERK 
MOANA LUTEY, LEGISLATIVE DIVISION STAFF JOYCE MURASHIGE, LAUREN SALDANA AND DELL 
YOSHIDA AND JOINING THE MEETING FROM THE DETERRENT OF CORPORATION COUNSEL IS 
ACTING CORPORATION COUNTY VICTORIA 11:04 TAKAYESU, AND FIRST DEPUTY COUNSEL IS 
SONYA TOMA. >> OPENING REMARKS THIS MORNING WILL BE PROVIDED BY MEMBER KAMA. >> 
THANK YOU, CHAIR. SO I JUST WANTED TO LET YOU ALL KNOW THAT I JUST GOT BACK FROM THE 
NATIONAL ASSOCIATION OF COUNTIES' LEGISLATIVE CONFERENCE IN WASHINGTON, D.C.. I WANT 
TO THANK MEMBER RAWLINS-FERNANDEZ FOR BEING THERE.\r\n\r\nYOU KNOW SOMETIMES WHEN 
YOU GO ON TRIPS BY YOURSELF, IT KIND OF FEELS LONELY AND WHEN YOU SEE SOMEONE ELSE 
FROM THE HOMETOWN, EVEN THOUGH THEY ARE ACROSS THE ROOM, DOWN THE END OF THE 
TABLE AT DINNER, IT'S JUST WARM TO KNOW THAT THEY ARE WITH YOU. I WAS REALLY 
GRATEFUL SHE WAS THERE. I MISSED ALL OF YOU THAT WEREN'T THERE, BUT HOPEFULLY AT THE 
NEXT ONE, WE CAN ALL BE THERE TOGETHER AND NOT VIOLATE ANY SUNSHINE LAWS. BUT ALSO,  
VERY GRATEFUL FOR THE MAYOR'S CHIEF OF STAFF FOR BEING THERE ALSO. SO WE SPENT A LOT 
OF TIME TALKING ABOUT SOME OF THE THINGS THAT WERE THEIR PRIORITIES AND SOME OF THE 
THINGS THAT WE TALKED ABOUT THAT OUR PRIORITIES. IT KIND OF FEELS REALLY GOOD TO 
file:///P|/OCC/LEG/Minutes/2023/230217/230217.txt[3/15/2023 9:35:06 AM]
TALK TO SOMEBODY WHAT YOUR PLANS ARE, WHAT YOUR FUTURE FOR OUR COUNTY AND WE'RE 
ALL TALKING THE SAME LANGUAGE, VERY WONDERFUL. ALSO, THERE WAS A LARGE 
CONTINGENCY FROM HAWAI'I COUNTIES, HAWAI'I COUNTY, KAUA'I COUNTY AND HONOLULU, CITY  
COUNCIL.\r\n\r\nSO ALTHOUGH I FELT -- I WAS GLAD WE WERE THERE. WE WERE THERE, MAUI NO 
KA 'OI. PRESIDENT BIDEN ADDRESSED THE EVERY YEAR WHEN WE GO THEY ALWAYS INVITE THE 
PRESIDENT. LAST TIME I WAS THERE, PRESIDENT THUMP WAS THERE AND SPOKE AND I KIND I 
WASN'T IMPRESSED, BUT I WAS IMPRESSED WITH PRESIDENT BIDEN, BECAUSE HE REMINDED US 
THAT THE COUNTIES GET FEDERAL DOLLARS, BECAUSE OF HIM. AND HE SHARED THE STORY, 
WHEN HE WAS A COUNTY COUNCIL MEMBER FROM DELAWARE, THAT EVERY TIME THEY HAD 
FEDERAL DOLLARS IT HAD TO GO THROUGH THE STATE, THE MUNICIPALITY AND WHATEVER IS 
LEFT, THEY GOT CRUMBS, SO WE TOLD HIMSELF ONE DAY, ONE DAY I'M GOING TO MAKE SURE 
THAT THE MONEY GOES DIRECTLY TO THE COUNTIES. YOU KNOW, THAT IS WHAT HE DID. THAT IS

MAOLI I WANT TO EXPRESS MY HOUSE, 23-42 SENT A HARM REDUCTION RESPONSE TO THE 
ONGOING TRAUMA HAWAIIANS FACE AS SURVIVORS OF COLONIZATION. IT'S A WAR AGAINST 
HAWAIIANS. IT'S INVASION OF HAWAIIAN LANDS. SETTLER COLONIZATION IS A HARM THAT 
HAPPENS WHEN NONPROFITS CRIMINALIZE HAWAIIANS ON HAWAIIAN LANDS. IT'S THE HARM 
THAT HAPPENS WHEN POLICE REMOVE HAWAIIANS FROM HAWAIIAN LANDS. IT'S THE HARM THAT 
HAPPENS TO HAWAIIANS. THE HARM THAT KEEPS HAPPENING TO HAWAIIANS AND THE HARM 
THAT TURNS HAWAIIANS INTO SURVIVORS OF AFFORDABILITY.\r\n\r\nAS A RESULT OF SETTLER 
COLONIALISM, HAWAIIANS CONSTITUTE A MERE 10% OF ETHNIC POPULATION AND OVER 50% OF 
THE HOUSELESS POPULATION IN HAWAI'I. LET ME REPEAT THAT ONE MORE TIME FOR FOLKS IN 
THE BACK, HAWAIIANS TODAY CONSTITUTE A MERE 10% OF THE ETHNIC POPULATION, OVER 50% 
OF THE HOUSELESS POPULATION IN HAWAI'I. THIS IS THE HARM OF SETTLER COLONIALISM AND 
THE WAR ON HAWAIIANS. FIRST STEP FOR TAKING ACCOUNTABILITY FOR THE HARM IS NOT TO 
CRIMINALIZE AND REMOVE HAWAIIANS STRUGGLING TO STAY ON OUR LANDS. THE FIRST STEPS 
TO TAKING ACCOUNTABILITY FOR THE HARM IS NOT TO CALL THE POLICE TO HARASS AND 
ARREST HAWAIIANS, STRUGGLING TO STAY ON THEIR LANDS. THE FIRST STEP, THE FIRST STEP TO 
TAKING ACCOUNTABILITY FOR THE HARM IS NOT TO EXPEL HAWAIIANS FROM OUR LANDS, SO

CONVENTIONAL PRODUCE. MOST OF THE FARMERS WE SERVE USE ORGANIC PRACTICE BECAUSE 
THAT IS WHAT MOST LOCAL FARMERS ARE PRACTICE. ONE OF THE MOST COMMON INQUIRES TO

CUSTOMERS BECAUSE ORGANIC WINS. I GET CALLS FROM YONKER FARMERS LOOKING FOR LAND 
AND LAND LEASES WITH BIER IERS AND HAVE THE ADDED BARRIER THAT THE LAND COULD NOT

WANT TO FARM ORGANICALLY AND THE FARM PROGRAM AND FAMILY FARMER TRAINING 
PROGRAM, TOO, ARE ALL PUMPING OUT FARMERS WHO WANT TO FARM ORGANIC FARMLAND. AS 
WRITTEN, THIS BILL DOESN'T REQUIRE KULA AG PARK USERS TO BE CERTIFIED ORGANIC. THE BILL  
ON PAGE 10 SECTION S-1 CLEARLY DEFINES WHAT IS ALLOWED IN THE KULA AG PARK, AND IT'S 
THE EXACT SAME RULES FOR CERTIFIED ORGANIC FARMERS. IF YOU GOOGLE THE NATIONAL LIST 
OF ALLOWED AND PROHIBITED SUBSTANCES IT COMES UP.\r\n\r\nI CAN ANSWER QUESTIONS ON 
WHAT HAD A MEANS IF YOU HAVE AND BASICALLY REFERS TO FEDERAL LAWING AND SAYS 
ANYTHING PROHIBITED IN ORGANIC FARMING IS ALSO PROHIBITED IN PHASE 2 OF THE KULA AG 
PARK. THAT WAY WE GET THE INTENT AND THE PRACTICES UNDER THE ORGANIC LABEL 
WITHOUT REQUIRING EVERY FARMER TO BE CERTIFIED. SIDE NOTE, IT'S ALSO THE SAME

TO OUR AINA, THAT HAVE BEEN DISPOSSESSED. IT WAS A SYSTEMATIC DISPOSSESSION. OUR 
PEOPLE WERE LITERALLY REMOVED FROM THE LANDS. IN SOME INSTANCES, PEOPLE WERE SENT 
TO KALAUPAPA, WHO DID NOT HAVE HANSON'S DISEASE AND IN THAT TIME THEY WERE SENT 
AWAY, THEIR LANDS WERE SUDDENLY GIVEN TO THE PLANTATION. WE HEAR STORY AFTER 
STORY AFTER STORY OF DISPOSSESSION FROM OUR LAND. WE ALSO HAD INDOCTRINATION, 
ANOTHER PART OF SETTLER COLONIALISM AND IT LEAD TO DEEP INTERNALIZED RACISM. THAT IS 
THE PART WHERE THEY LIED TO US ABOUT WHO THEY ARE.\r\n\r\nMY PARENT'S GENERATION AND 
THEIR PARENT'S GENERATION AND PARENT'S GENERATIONS WERE TOLD HAWAIIANS ARE STUPID, 
LAZY, AND CAN'T LEARN -- DIRTY. SQUATTERS. BUT I'M HERE TO DELAY THAT THE AGE OF LUNA 
IS OVER. WE ARE NOT DOING PLANTATION POLITICS ANY MORE. IT'S VIOLENCE. FORCING THIS 
PROJECT IS THE EXACT SAME THING PLANTATION DID. IT'S REPEATING HISTORY.\r\n\r\nWE'RE 
HEARING THE SAME TROUPES.  THAT THE FAMILIES ARE DIRTY. THAT THEY ARE NOT TAKING CARE  
OF THE LAND. THAT THEY ARE SQUATTERS. THAT THEY ARE STUPID, THAT THEY DON'T KNOW

RESOLUTION NO. 23-41 URGING THE ADMINISTRATION TO ISSUE A REQUEST FOR PROPOSALS TO 
ADMINISTER A HOMEOWNER ASSISTANTS FUND PROGRAM UNDER THE AMERICAN RES CUE PLAN 
ACT ACT OF 2021. WHEREAS, ORDINANCE 5332 TOOK EFFECT JANUARY 24TH, 2022, RECOGNIZING A 
GRANT OF MORE THAN $8 MILLION FOR THE PURPOSE OF PREVENTING HOMEOWNER MORTGAGE 
DELINQUENCIES, DEFAULTS, FORFEITURES, LOSS OF UTILITIES, OR HOME ENERGY SERVICES, AND 
DISPLACEMENTS OF HOMEOWNERS EXPERIENCING FINANCIAL HARDSHIP, ACCORDING TO THE 
FORMER BUDGET DIRECTOR'S CORRESPONDENCE DATED DECEMBER 30TH, 2021, INCLUDING THE 
LIMITED-TERM APPOINTMENT OF A FULL-TIME STAFF POSITION; AND WHEREAS, SECTION 3206 OF 
THE AMERICAN RESCUE PLAN ACT OF 2021 ALLOWS FOR A HOMEOWNER ASSISTANCE FUND 
PROGRAM; AND WHEREAS, THE HOMEOWNER ASSISTANCE FUND CAN BE USED MORE BROADLY 
THAN THE COMMUNITY DEVELOPMENT BLOCK GRANT PROGRAM FUNDS ADMINISTERED BY MAUI 
ECONOMIC OPPORTUNITY, INC.; AND WHEREAS, A REQUEST FOR PROPOSALS TO ADMINISTER A 
HOMEOWNER ASSISTANCE FUND PROGRAM HAS NOT BEEN ISSUED, EVEN THOUGH THE $8,060,550 
GRANT NEEDS TO BE EXPENDED ENTIRELY BY SEPTEMBER 30TH, 2025; AND WHEREAS, ALL OTHER 
COUNTIES IN THE STATE HAVE ISSUED A HOMEOWNER ASSISTANCE FUND PROGRAM LEAVING 
file:///P|/OCC/LEG/Minutes/2023/230217/230217.txt[3/15/2023 9:35:06 AM]
